<userid>108744312439460682853</userid><rating>5<//rating><Text>Literally so good. I was here for dinner 2 days ago and still thinking about it. I shared the fried chicken and drunken noodles with a friend and we left SO happy. Noodles were generous with lots of good veggies and chicken. Usually I pick through stuff like that but I was too focused on shoving it in my mouth to do that. The fried chicken with lime sauce was so good I saved a tiny bit at the corner of my plate to end my meal with and let me tell you, GREAT DECISION. The sales that came with it was also great. The magnum opus, however, was definitely their homemade chili garlic sauce. They sell it at the restaurant and I knew from the first bite I wasn't leaving without a container of it. It was so flavorful and a great level of spice. I can't wait to cook with it at home.

Also the restaurant is family ran and the two sisters waiting on us were so sweet and welcoming. Honestly if you only have one meal in Fort Bragg, I would recommend here.<//Text><name>Charles Hawthorne</name><Gmap_id>0x808035790e7a0cad:0x14badc2acc9de2da< /Gmap_id></record></dataset><record>

< text>
If you want good Thai, this is the right place. If you want a fusion restaurant, you'll want to look elsewhere. The "fusion" is your typical mixture of Thai and Laotian dishes. With the exception of a couple items, everything on the menu is exactly what you would expect to find at a normal Thai restaurant. The food is good, and I would eat here again. It's just not what I expected based on the name.< /text>

< Text>
Excellent Thai restaurant. Waitress was prompt, polite, and professional. Food arrived quickly, was of high quality, and was perfectly seasoned. Prices are fair and portions are generous. I ordered the Thai Basil (Pad Graw Prow), chicken, Thai hot. The chicken pieces were juicy and on the larger size, which I prefer, and the chili sauce was sweet with enough of a syrupy character to nicely coat the vegetables and chicken. There were plenty of chopped Bird peppers to get the heat level up, although this dish today was not what I'd consider a "10" on the heat scale, more like 8.5. I feel confident that they could make it hotter if requested.

This is a young restaurant, and it warmed my heart to see lots of people coming in to eat as we were eating. I want to eat here again on my next visit to Fort Bragg!< /Text>

<Text>THIS IS THE ONE!  KIME Performance helped me recover from shoulder joint replacement surgery in Spring 2019 after nearly 20 years of suffering caused by a January 2000 mountain biking crash in the woods surrounding Folsom Lake.   I had visited other area physical therapists prior to this surgery and following other surgeries, but I never saw results like I experienced at KIME Performance.

While I know the joint replacement surgery itself was key, nearly every muscle in my upper body had wasted away from not being being able to exercise during the nearly 20 years since the crash.  The experienced care I received at KIME Performance (located in Mini's House of Pain) nursed my body back to life and helped make me a whole person again.  The simple exercises work and are easy to at home or any gym.  Some of the exercises are so much fun that I do them on the floor in the family room at home while watching TV with the family.

< Review>
The food I ordered were heavily seasoned with MSG.  The hot & sour soup tasted like it had soap in it.  The black bean noodle didn't taste right.  I have been a regular customer there for a long time but it seems the MSG was the main ingredient for most of the dishes.  My wife got sick right after eating their food and my mouth was really dry due to MSG.  We ordered 6 dishes but had to toss them out.  Please be sure to tell them no MSG in any dishes.   The customer service was great but the food was salty and MSG is used for flavoring but has been associated with various forms of toxicity.  It's unhealthy to consume MSG.</Review>

<time>1558073852489< /time><Rate>4<//Rate><Review>Searching through the city on Christmas day to see what was open and found this place! (I know most people think that all Chinese restaurants are open Christmas day but surprisingly some of them were closed in the area).

Really convenient that you can put yourself on the yelp waitlist because you'll be pretty squished if you want to wait inside because there isn't much of a waiting area, and it's pretty warm when it's crowded.

To start of the meal, got soymilk and sticky rice rolls. Sticky rice rolls were wrapped in plastic and cut. Good amount of dried pork and fried bread inside inside the roll. Also tried the potstickers, crab XLB, and shanghai fried noodles. The XBL and potstickers have thick skin, so if you aren't a fan of that, this place might not be the place for you. Potstickers were fried nicely on the bottom and the meat was juicy inside! Crab XLB had tender, fresh juicy meat inside with flavorful broth. Noodles were thick cut, chewy and delicious!

Overall decent chinese dumpling place, parking can be a pain to find in this area, so be prepared!</Review>< pictures>

Catching up on my reviews Pre Covid!

Food: 4/5
Service: 3/5
Ambiance: 3/5
Overall: A good option for Shanghainese dumplings

The extended review...

Food:

Soup Dumplings: 4/5 - Juicy and meaty like most

Snow Pea Shoots: 4/5 - My favorite Chinese vegetable with a tender yet crunchy bite

Beef and Sting Beans: 4/5 - A good option when you want meat and veggies in the same dish

Ambiance: Standard fair when it comes to Chinese restaurants

Service:  Same as the ambiance</review>

<Text>Dumpling Kitchen is a hidden gem among the SF Sunset District! Came across this place when finding good restaurants to eat with my friends. We were craving Xiao Long Bao Â∞èÁ±†ÂåÖ, known as the soup dumpling and happen to have found one around the area. Not too long of a wait, since we found that they also do Yelp Waitlist! Keep in mind that this restaurant only accepts debit card or cash unfortunately but luckily most people carry a debit card at least! Great to support a family owned business!

My friends and I ordered the A1. Xiao Long Bao that came with 10 soup dumplings. Definitely recommend dipping the soup dumplings in vinegar and a little soy sauce if you like a little base to the vinegar. We also ordered the Shanghai Chow Mein and the Pea Sprout Veggies, a classic Chinese vegetable dish that goes great with Xiao Long Baos. Xiao Long Baos were delicious as you pop them into your mouth and the flavor and soup explode inside with the tender meat wrapped up as a surprise. The Shanghai Chow Mein was fantastic since I love noodles and the noodles were thick with chicken and vegetables mixed into it. And finally the Pea Sprout Veggies are a classic vegetable dish to fill up your tummy with savory goodness.

The servers are super friendly and helped suggest popular dishes for us, and speak English, Cantonese Chinese. or Mandarin Chinese. Price was super affordable and cheap! I‚Äôll definitely come back with family and friends to support this local community business!<//Text><Pics>[{'url': ['https://lh5.googleusercontent.com/p/AF1QipOnjAPkh4ZWytJn1Qirt-r2xdmmqAqqrzOHdRWj=w150-h150-k-no-p']}, {'url': ['https://lh5.googleusercontent.com/p/AF1QipNJG3l0pva-xaRxfws_-1YCvl3ZTpfWYWjhgzsy=w150-h150-k-no-p']}, {'url': ['https://lh5.googleusercontent.com/p/AF1QipO-u1vxsqkfeDAhNVAzjG2oDIsdudtSI_Rn7yeB=w150-h150-k-no-p']}]<//Pics>< response>

< Review>
Pretty solidly good food - friend and I went to lunch and ordered 4 dishes.  The hot and sour soup was pretty tasty.  The Shanghai style dumpling with soup in the middle was better than average but certainly not comparable to ones at Din Tai Fung.  Prices were a littler higher than you might expect, but the place is nice/clean and service was attentive.  Read that this place gets crowded so we went at about 2PM on a weekday and place was mostly empty :)

Biggest downer is the place does NOT take credit cards.  We may opt to go to other similar restaurants next time that do take credit cards.<//Review>

< review>
Our usual dumpling place is Kingdom of Dumplings, but I wanted to try a new place.  We showed up around 2 pm on a Saturday and the place was pretty packed.  We got a table quickly.  The menu of stir fried items surpassed that number of possible dumpling combinations.  This place strictly has pork dumplings, not chicken and limited to cabbage filling.  We got several dishes; thread pulled fried bread, chicken and spinach noodle soup, twice cooked  pork belly with leek, Shanghai steamed dumplings, and fish in black bean sauce.  My daughter ate most of the fried bread, you dip in condense milk which gives it bit of sweetness.  The Shanghai dumplings were ok, not too great.  The chicken and spinach noodle soup was very flavorful and the noodles chewy.  All the dishes were sold and good.  Looking around, people came here and ordered very different dishes.  Someone had a plate of chicken wings that looked really good, so I'm going to try that next time we go back.</review>

Started off with a Nice and warm soy milk and complimentary roasted peanuts. Dumpling xiao long bao was warm with juicy sauce in the middle. When you eat it be careful because the inside is very hot. Make sure you drink the soup while eating the dumplings. The rice cake noodles dish with chewy with shredded pork and veges. I also ordered a sweet rice roll for dessert later. All for only around $20 and there was leftovers for Togo too. Very yummy and satisfying.Ôªø<//Text>

<user_id>114423743672147906343<//user_id><text>Since Kingdom of Dumpling doesn't open until 11 or 11:30 on Sundays, we walked down the street until we stumbled upon Dumpling Kitchen.

Shanghai soup dumplings were done surprisingly well here and from what I recall, the price point is a tad lower too, so you get ten squishy balls of joy for $8. The wrapper was just right since you could see the pork through it, but no soup leakage at all!

I loved their version of Shanghai style fried noodles, partially because of the excellent portion size. Getting the dumplings and the noodle dish was more than enough for two hungry dudes.

Would love to try their egg puffs next time.

Wish they had vinegar handy on the tables!</text>< GmapID>

<review>I love dumplings, and this was the next place on my dumpling bucket list in the city. There were two of us, and we ordered the Shanghai dumplings, the pork dumplings in chili oil and the pork and napa cabbage dumplings.

Shanghai dumplings: Good texture, with a good amount of soup inside, but to me, the flavor was lacking.

Pork dumplings in chili oil: Again, the texture of these was great - perfectly steamed. The flavor of the dumpling was good, but the chili oil that comes on the table was better than the oil that the dumplings were cooked in. They did, however, include slices of raw garlic which gave the dish a pretty good kick to it.

Pork and napa cabbage: These were my favorite. Really good flavor and texture, and went really well with the chili oil on the table.

While these weren't my favorite dumplings in the city, I would come back again because the food was decent, service was fast and the meal was cheap (a little over $20!). I did see someone eating beef noodle soup and would try that next time I go.<//review><pictures>None</pictures><user_id>112444094149673294405< /user_id></record></dataset><record>
<gmap_id>0x808f7d835ad0d52f:0x61768a5c80a9e9dc< /gmap_id><Pics>None</Pics><date>1518917306286<//date><UserId.>116838550636744514823</UserId.><review>I hadn't been back since almost 5 years ago, but I'm glad I returned.

There was a line at lunch on this lunar new year and it was worth the wait. Tea came quickly and the service was friendly, helpful, and fairly efficient, despite the packed restaurant.

In addition to veg steamed dumplings and scallion pancakes (both still winners, though the scallion pancake isn't really good value), we tried the mu shu vegetable.

The mu shu vegetable (without egg) came on a big oval plate with little pieces of broccoli in addition to the more standard veggies. I felt so lucky! We received six pancakes and I appreciated that they were thick and therefore didn't break, as so many do at other Chinese restaurants. The hoison sauce was thick and tasty, so the whole package was good and yummy.<//review>< user_name>

< Text>
Ordered the burnin Brock and the breakfast sausage hot dog. The internet and overall ambiance of the restaurant felt hip and classy. Service was friendly and fairly fast!

Was not a fan of the Burnin Brock. The chicken sausage was really dry and crumbly. Furthermore, felt like the fried avocado didn't really compliment the flavor and vibe of the hot dog. On the other hand, the breakfast sausage was juicy and delicious. I love the toppings and the duck egg was a great addition. Furthermore, the buns here are outstandingly soft and they have a wide selection of beers that are worth checking out!

I don't recommend coming during lunch time, came here for the curry fries and sausage platter but they don't serve those until 5pm. Will revisit to try those two dishes again!</Text>

<user_id>100249539677162904250</user_id><name>Nei Ng</name>< Time>
1468338696371<//Time>
<Rate>4< /Rate>< review>
We had a pretty large group here last night for a couple of friends' birthdays. For the value, Dumpling Kitchen was pretty good. It's no Michelin star restaurant but a satisfying combination of price, portion, and flavor.

XLB - The skins were way better than I expected at this price point. Their texture was smooth with the right amount of firm chewiness. Just from looking at them, the fine folds at the top was a good sign that the skins would be thin and delicate. They also didn't break open when picked up with chopstick. Not much to complain about there. The stuffing was not the best but still decent for a low end restaurant. The texture of the pork was on the grittier side, and I thought it could've had more ginger and green onions mixed in for more brightness. The broth was similar to the pork stuffing in that it could be brighter and bolder, but it still had good body and was seasoned with enough salt . The broth was also on the fattier side, which doesn't bother me, but I know some people out there prefer cleaner XLB broths.

Braised Pork Belly with Pickled Vegetables - You can tell this restaurant probably isn't run by Shanghainese people because of kitchen staff yelling at each other in Cantonese, and this is reflected in some of the menu items. This braised pork belly dish is a traditional Hakka classic from southern China, far from Shanghai. Dumpling Kitchen's rendition is actually pretty good. The pork belly was tender, and the sauce was a good balance of sweetness and pickled earthiness. My favorite place to order this is at Hakka Restaurant in the Outer Richmond. If I had to compare the two, Hakka's sauce is thicker and richer with a more complex spice mixture. There's a slight orange peel flavor in Hakka's that separates it from the rest. Despite not being as good as Hakka's, I would have no qualms with getting the pork belly here.

Green Onion Pancakes - Not really my cup of tea. They have the lighter and fluffier version of green onion pancakes, and I didn't think it had much green onion flavor. It kinda just tasted doughy. The crispy and layered green onion pancakes are way better.

Vegetarian Potstickers - There was a vegetarian in our group so we had an order of vegetarian potstickers. I was kinda surprised because they turned out to be pretty tasty. I probably liked them more than the pork and chive dumplings. There's a good amount of shiitake mushrooms to give it a lot of umami and earthy flavors. They also put in dried tofu (doufu gon), and it's firmer texture and five spice flavor paired well with the other ingredients in the stuffing.

Noodles with Black Bean Sauce - Not good. Sauce was not very savory and didn't taste black bean-y. Noodles were mushy and gross. Skip this.

Egg Puffs (Sah Yong) - Freshly fried and really delicious. They were light, airy, and full of eggy goodness. If I had to complain about something, it's that instead of surrounding the donuts in sugar, it's just poured all on top of the donuts. I just rolled the donut around to get the sugar everywhere.< /review>

We ordered:

XLB Shanghai-style steamed pork dumplings (10pcs) - they were DELICIOUS!!!
Shanghai-style pan-fried pork buns (8pcs) - Meh, would not order these again

Shanghai-style green onion pancake - YUM! Crispy, onions, light, fluffy!!!
Beijing-style sweet buns (4pcs) - Meh. We ordered steamed but got fried. Even still, just meh.

This is a good place for 4 or more people to come and dine with portion sizing. We ordered way too much food so that we could try a bunch of things. We'd definitely share a table again, just hopefully not the round table at the back (my hubs had to get up 3 times so the food delivery hand truck could make it to the kitchen).
